25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25839-2" target="اضعفهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n25840"/></foreign>, (S, O, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِضْعَافٌ</foreign>; (S, Msb;) all signify the same; (S, K;) i. e. <hi rend="ital">He doubled it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made it double,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">two-fold;</hi> (O, K;) [and <hi rend="ital">trebled it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made it treble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">three-fold;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">redoubled it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made it several-fold,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manyfold;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">multiplied it;</hi> for] Kh says, <foreign lang="ar">التَّضْعِيفُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">the adding to</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">so as to make</hi> it <hi rend="ital">double,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">two-fold;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">more</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">treble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">threefold;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">several-fold,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">many-fold</hi>]; (S, O, Msb;) and so <foreign lang="ar">الإِضْعَافُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">المُضَاعَفَةُ</foreign>; (S, Msb;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25839-3" target="ضَعَفَهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, without teshdeed, signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">ضاعفهُ</foreign>. (Ham p. 257.) The saying, in the Kur [xxxiii. 30], <foreign lang="ar">يُضَاعَفْ لَهَا العَذَابُ ضِعْفَيْنِ</foreign>, (Mgh, O, K,) in which AA read   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25839-4" target="يُضَعَّفْ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (TA,) accord. to AO, (Mgh, O,) means, <hi rend="ital">The punishment shall be made to her three punishments;</hi> (Mgh, O, K;) for, he says, she is to be punished once; and when the punishment is doubled twofold, [or is repeated twice,] the one becomes three: (TA:) he adds, (O,) and the tropical meaning of <foreign lang="ar">يُضَاعَفْ</foreign> (<foreign lang="ar">مَجَازُ يُضَاعَفْ</foreign> [for which <foreign lang="ar">مَجازٌ يُضَاعَفُ</foreign> is erroneously put in the CK]) is two things' being added to a thing so that it becomes three: (O, K:) but Az disapproves this, saying that it is peculiar to the tropical and the common conventional speech, whereas the skilled grammarians state the meaning to be, <hi rend="ital">she shall be punished with twice the like of the punishment of another;</hi> (Mgh;) [so that it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">the punishment shall be doubled to her,</hi> made <hi rend="ital">two-fold;</hi> and in like manner] Ibn-'Arafeh explains it as meaning <hi rend="ital">she shall have two shares of punishment.</hi> (O.) <foreign lang="ar">فَيُضَاعِفُهُ لَهُ أَضْعَافًا كَثِيرَةً</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And He will multiply it to him many-fold,</hi> or, as some read, <foreign lang="ar">فَيُضَاعِفَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">that He may multiply it,</hi>] is another phrase occurring in the Kur [ii. 246]. (O, TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25839-5" target="أَضْعَفْتُ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>الثَّوَابَ لِلْقَوْمِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I doubled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">multiplied, the recompense to the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party</hi>]. (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25839-6" target="أُضْعِفَ" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>القَوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party, had a doubling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">multiplying,</hi> [of their recompense, &amp;c.,] <hi rend="ital">made to them;</hi> (Msb;) [and so, app., <foreign lang="ar">أَضْعَفُوا</foreign>; (see <foreign lang="ar">مُضْعِفٌ</foreign>;)] <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ضُوعِفَ لَهُمْ</foreign>. (S, O, K.)    </entryFree>29:Ta23,<entryFree id="n25842" key="ضَعْفٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ضَعْفٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> an inf. n. of 1, like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25842-1" target="ضُعْفٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n25843"/></foreign>, (S, *  O, *  Msb, K,) [both, when used as simple substs., signifying <hi rend="ital">Weakness, feebleness,</hi> &amp;c.,] but some say that the former is in the judgment or opinion, and the latter in the body; (O, Msb, K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25842-2" target="ضَعَفٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n25845"/></foreign> signifies the same, (IAar, K, TA,) and is in the body and also in the judgment or opinion and the intellect. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَعْفُ التَّأْلِيفِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Weakness of construction, in language,</hi>] is <hi rend="ital">such a construction of the members of a sentence as is contrary to the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">generally approved</hi>] <hi rend="ital">rules of syntax;</hi> as when a pronoun is introduced before its noun with respect to the actual order of the words and the order of the sense [in a case in which the pronoun is affixed to the agent in a verbal proposition]; for instance, in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ غُلَامُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدًا</foreign> [“ His, ” i. e. Zeyd's, “ young man beat Zeyd ”]. (KT.) When the pronoun is affixed to the objective complement, as in <foreign lang="ar">خَافَ رَبَّهُ عُمَرُ</foreign> [“ 'Omar feared his Lord ”] such introduction of it is common: (I'Ak p. 128:) and it is [universally] allowable when the pronoun is of the kind called <foreign lang="ar">ضَمِيرُ الشَّأْنِ</foreign>, as in <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّهُ زَيْدٌ قَائِمٌ</foreign>; or <foreign lang="ar">ضَمِيرُ رُبَّ</foreign>, as in <foreign lang="ar">رُبَّهُ رَجُلًا لَقِيتُهُ</foreign>; or <foreign lang="ar">ضَمِيرُ نِعْمَ</foreign>, as in <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَهُ رَجُلًا زَيْدٌ</foreign>. (Kull p. 56.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [In the CK, a signification belonging to <foreign lang="ar">ضُعْف</foreign> is assigned to <foreign lang="ar">ضَعْف</foreign>.]    </entryFree>2a:T1e79,<entryFree id="n25844" key="ضِعْفُ الشَّىْءِ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ضِعْفُ الشَّىْءِ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> signifies <hi rend="ital">The like of the thing,</hi> (AO, Zj, S, O, Msb, K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">that doubles it</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يُضْعِفُهُ</foreign>); (Zj, TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفَاهُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">twice the like of it;</hi> (AO, S, O, Msb, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">أَضْعَافُهُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">the likes of it:</hi> (S, Msb:) <foreign lang="ar">الضِّعْفُ</foreign> in the [proper] language of the Arabs means <hi rend="ital">the like:</hi> this is the original signification: (Az, Msb:) and (K, TA, but in CK “ or, ”) then, by a later [and conventional] usage, (Az, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">the like and more, the addition being unlimited:</hi> (Az, Msb, K:) one says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفُ هٰذَا</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">This is the like of this:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَانِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفَاهُ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">These two are twice the like of it:</hi> and it is allowable in the language of the Arabs to say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ضِعْفُهُ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">This is twice the like</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the double</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of it,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">thrice the like</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the treble</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of it,</hi> [and <hi rend="ital">more,</hi>] because the <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْف</foreign> is an unlimited addition: (Az, Msb: [and the like is said in the O, on the authority of Az:]) and one says, <foreign lang="ar">لَكَ ضِعْفُهُ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">Thou shalt have twice the like of it,</hi> (Zj, O, K,) using the sing. form, though the dual form is better, (Zj, O,) and meaning also <hi rend="ital">thrice the like of it,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">more without limit:</hi> (K:) and <foreign lang="ar">الاِثْنَانِ ضِعْفُ الوَاحِدِ</foreign> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">الاثنان</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">is the double of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الواحد</foreign>]: (M and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">ثنى</foreign>:) and if one say in his will, <foreign lang="ar">أَعْطُوهُ ضِعْفَ نَصِيبِ وَلَدِى</foreign>, twice the like of the share of his child is given to him; and if he say <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفَيْهِ</foreign>, thrice the like thereof is given to him; so that if the share of the son be a hundred, he [the legatee] is given two hundred in the former case, and three hundred in the latter case; for the will is made to accord with the common conventional language, not with the niceties of the [proper] language: (Az, Msb: [and the like is said, but less fully, in the Mgh:]) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَضْعَافٌ</foreign> only. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">إِذًا لَأَذَقْنَاكَ ضِعْفَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَيَاةِ وَضِعْفَ المَمَاتِ</foreign>, in the Kur [xvii. 77], means <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفَ العَذَابِ حَيًّا وَمَيِّتًا</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفَ عَذَابِ</foreign> 
                  <pb n="1792"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَيَاةِ وَضِعْفَ عَذَابِ المُمَاتِ</foreign>, (O, Jel,) i. e. [<hi rend="ital">In that case we would assuredly have made thee to taste</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the like</hi> [or, as some explain it, <hi rend="ital">the double</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the punishment</hi> of others <hi rend="ital">in the present world and</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the like</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the double thereof</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in the world to come:</hi> (Jel:) [Sgh adds, app. on the authority of Ibn-'Arafeh,] the meaning is, the punishment of others should be made two-fold, or more, (<foreign lang="ar">يُضَاعَف</foreign>,) to thee, because thou art a prophet. (O.) In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">فَأُولَائِكَ لَهُمْ جَزَآءُ ٱلضِّعْفِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِمَا عَمِلُوا</foreign>, in the Kur [xxxiv. 36], by <foreign lang="ar">الضِّعْفِ</foreign> is meant <foreign lang="ar">الأضْعَافِ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">For these shall be the recompense of the likes for what they have done</hi>]; and it is most properly held to denote ten of the likes thereof, because of the saying in the Kur [vi. 161], “ Whoso doth that which is good, for him shall be ten of the likes thereof. ” (O.) In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">فَآتِهِمْ عَذَابًا ضِعْفًا</foreign>, in the Kur [vii. 36], by <foreign lang="ar">ضِعْفًا</foreign> is meant <foreign lang="ar">مُضَاعَفًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Therefore do Thou recompense them with a doubled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a double, punishment</hi>]: <foreign lang="ar">عَذَابٌ ضِعْفٌ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">a punishment as though doubled, one part of it upon another.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَضْعَافُ الكِتَابِ</foreign> means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The interspaces of the lines,</hi> (S, O, K, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">of the margin,</hi> (S, O,) or and <hi rend="ital">of the margins,</hi> (K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">of the writing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">book:</hi> (S, O, K, TA:) so in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">وَقَّعَ</foreign>

(O, K.)    </entryFree>2d:T78a,<entryFree id="n25853" key="مُضْعِفٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مُضْعِفٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> A man <hi rend="ital">whose beast,</hi> (S, K, and Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">كفأ</foreign>,) or <hi rend="ital">whose camel,</hi> (O,) <hi rend="ital">is weak,</hi> (S, Mgh, O, K,) or <hi rend="ital">untractable.</hi> (O.) Hence the saying of ' Omar, <foreign lang="ar">المُضْعِفُ أَمِيرٌ عَلَى أَصْحَابِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He whose beast is weak,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">untractable, is ruler over his companions</hi>]; (O, K;) i. e. in journeying; (O;) because they go his pace. (O, K.) And the saying, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">يَرُدُّ مُشِدُّهُمْ عَلَى مُضْعِفِهِمْ</foreign> [expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">شد</foreign>]. (Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">كفأ</foreign>.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">فَأُولَائِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُضْعِفُونَ</foreign>, in the Kur [xxx. 38], means <hi rend="ital">These are they who shall have their recompense doubled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">multiplied:</hi> (Az, Bd, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">those who double,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">multiply, their recompense</hi> (Bd, Jel) and <hi rend="ital">their possessions,</hi> (Bd,) by the blessing of their almsgiving: (Bd, Jel: *) but some read <foreign lang="ar">المُضْعَفُونَ</foreign>. (Bd.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">المُضْعِفُ</foreign> also signifies <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ فَشَتْ ضَيْعَتُهُ وَكَثُرَتْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He whose property has become wide-spread and abundant</hi>]. (Ibn-' Abbád, O, L, K.)    </entryFree>2e:T749,<entryFree id="n25854" key="أَرْضٌ مُضَعَّفَةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَرْضٌ مُضَعَّفَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Land upon which a weak rain has fallen:</hi> (Ibn-'Abbád, O, K:) and [in like manner]   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25854-1" target="مَضْعُوفٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n25856"/></foreign> signifies a place <hi rend="ital">upon which has fallen only a little,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">weak, rain.</hi> (O in art. <foreign lang="ar">رك</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">المُضَعَّفُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">One of the arrows used in the game of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُيْسِر</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">that has no share,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion, allotted to it;</hi> as though it were disabled from having a share (<foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّهُ <ref cref="n25854-2" target="ضُعِّفَ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ نَصِيبٌ</foreign>): (TA:) <hi rend="ital">the second of the arrows termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغُفْلُ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">that have no notches, and to which is assigned</hi> [<hi rend="ital">no portion and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">no fine:</hi> these being added only to give additional weight to the collection of arrows from fear of occasioning suspicion [of foul play]. (Lh, M.) [See <foreign lang="ar">السَّفِيحُ</foreign>.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">ضَعَفٌ</foreign>.
